COLOhBIA
FIFTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FINANCIRA DEL CARIBE
Statement of Policies and Procedures
1.        The Corporaci6n shall direct its energies toward financing the
Colombian private sector, giving special attention to the follow-
ing economic sectors:  manufacturing, agriculture, mining, tourism
and fishing.
2.        The Corporacion shall devote its efforts chiefly te, the forma-ricn,
expansion or financing of enterprises intended to increase agricul-
tural production, especially of exportable products; the industriali-
zation of food production, preserving, canning, etc.; the increasing
of trade in the Caribbean area and the developing of European markets
for Caribbean exports; the development and exploitation of fisheries
in Colombian waters; the integration at the national level of tne
assembling industries; and the tourist trade as a source of fore-gn
exchange for Colombia in the area of the Atlantic Coast and the $an
Andr6s archipelago, for which purpose, the Corporacion shal?! have, in
addition to its capital and credit resources, technical assstance
drawing on the traditional experience of the Dutch associa-ec In re-
gions with geographic features similar to Colombiats, such as kr'uonesia,
the Netherlands Antilles and Surinam.
The Corporaci6n shall direct its activities in accordance with the
provisional Decree 2369 of 1960 and any additions or amend-
ments thereto, and the economic policy of the National Government.
3.        In the pursuance of its corporate object, the Corporacion will attempt
to give priority to the following operations:
(a)    Promote the formation and organization of industrial, agricultural
or mining enterprises which, after the necessary feasibility
studies, will seek to ensure both Colombia's economic develop-
ment and a reasonable return on investment.
(b)    Participate in the capital of enterprises promoted directly by
itself or in those in the process of expansion. The Coroora-
cion can do this either be direct subscription of shares or by
granting lines of credit that can, at the option of the Cor-
poracion, be converted into shares of the borrowing company.
(c)    Grant credit at terms not exceeding 15 years to manufacturing,
agriculture, livestock, mining, transportation, tourism and
other enterprises authorized by Colombian law that seek to pro-
mote Colombia's economic development.  The Corporacion shall
supervise every credit operation from the time of the loan
application throughout the life of the credit.
(d)    Stimulate Colombian exports, through specialized lines of credit,



APPETDIX G
Annex8
Page 2
COLOMBIA
FIFTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FINANCIERA DEL CARIBE
giving Colombian manufacturers access to credit in foreign
exchange with which to purchase imported raw materials for
the manufacture of products to be exported.
It.      The Corporacion shall promote the development of the Colombian capital
market as follows:
(a)      It shall seek association with foreign capital.
(b)      It shall attempt to obtain lines of credit abroad, in order
to use such funds for the purposes described in the Corpora-
ci6n's general credit policy.
(c)      It shall act as an intermediary, on commission, in placing
securities issued by private Colombian enterprises, with a
view to attracting private investors.
(d)      It shall issue bonds and other securities authorized by law,
taking full advantage of its own standing and the confidence
it enjoys on the domestic economic scene, and shall, in addi-
tion, act as an intermediary .or issuing and placing on the
market certificates representing rights or securities received
in trust.
5.       It shall seek to guide its financial policy in accordance with principles
that will make it an effective agent of economic development. To that
end, the Corporacion shall operate in accordance with the following rules:
(a)      It shall use its economic development reserves and other resources
of its own for capital investments (subject to the limitations
set forth in paragraph VII) and for loans with a maturity of
five or more years. It shall constantly aim to increase its
investments in medium and long-term credits and in capital invest-
ments, subject to the restriction in paragraph VII.
(b)      The total direct or indirect credits granted by the Corporacion
to any natural or juridical person and the guarantees it extends
for any one person may not exceed one tenth of the Corporacion's
paid-in capital and legal reserve.
The total obligation of any one person to the Corporacion, in-
cluding guarantees, may exceed that limit, but may not exceed
25A of the paid-in capital and legal reserve, when it arises from
documentary credits and the respective documents are endorsed to
the Corporaci6n without reservation, or when such obligations, to
the extent that they exceed one tenth but not 25% of the paid-in
capital and legal reserve of the Corporaci6n, are backed by real
guarantees of a commercial value that is sufficient to adequately
cover the total obligation so guaranteed.



APPENDIX G
Annex 8
Page 3
COLOMBIA
FIFTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FINANCIERA DEL CARIBE
In addition to the foregoing restrictions, the total financing
to a single beneficiary for investment, credit, guarantee or
other credit facilities shall not exceed 25% of the Corporacion's
net assets.
(c)     The Corporacion shall pursue a conservative dividend policy
that will enable it to build up adequate reserves while dis-
tributing a proper return anong its stockholders at the proper
time. The Corporacion shall allot part of its net profits to
reserves each year. The allotments to reserves shall be made
in a such a way as to permit the constitution of total reserves
equivalent in quality and amount to the Corporaci6n's credit
and investment portfolio.
(d)     The Corporacion shall neither contract, nor assume nor guarantee
any debit if, at the time or as a result of that operation, the
total indebtedness contracted, assumed or guaranteed by the Cor-
poraci6n and still outstanding exceeds 20 times its net paid-in
capital and legal reserves.
(e)     The maturities of the Corporacion's assets shall be equal to or
shorter than those of its liabil'ties.
(f)     The Corporacion shall not normally effect operations of less than
one hundred thousand* save in exceptional circumstances.
6.      As far as possible, the staff of the Corporacion shall provide its cus-
tomers with technical assistance, so that when they are preparing studies
or projects they can rely on adequate guidance from the Corporacion or
from other competent institutions recormended by it.
7.      Save in situtations of a temporary character, future participation by
the Corporaci6n in the capital of an enterprise shall never be so large
as to cause it to assume direct responsibility for managing the enterprise.
This means that the Corporaci6n's participation in the subscribed capital
of enterprises should not normally exceed 15% of such subscribed capital.
The total capital investments of the Corporaci6n shall not exceed the
value of its net paid-in capital and legal reserve.
The Corporacion shall try to protect itself adequately against any ex-
change risks that may arise from its operations.
*T.N.: Presumably Colombian pesos.



APPENDIX G
Annex 8-
Pige 4
CO-LOMiBIA
FTFTE FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FINANCIERA DEL CARIBE
10.      The Corporacion shall maintain a qualified staff for its managexaent
and particularly for technical, economic, and financial appraisal of
the projects to be financed and for supervision of those approved.
11.      The Corporacion shall maintain the contracts made with independent
public accountants to conduct the annual audit of its books and
accounts.
12.      Any decision on a matter in which any one of the directors has an
interest shall be taken solely by the other directors. The director
or directors involved shall take no part either in the discussion or
in the voting.
13.      The management of the Corporacion shall submit to the Board monthly
reports including:
(a)   investigation of new projects
(b)   progress on investments made
(c)   financial statements
(d)   portfolio in arrears
(e)   report on promotional activities
(f)   other matters having a major bearing on the Corporacion's financial
position and operations.

APPENDIX H
Page 1
CORPORACION FINANCIERA DE SANTANDER
INTRODUCTION
1.        Santander was formed in 1966 by a group of private and public
Colombian shareholders to finance and promote private enterprises in the
industrial, agricultural, mining and tourism sectors, particularly in the
Santander region. Santander's offices are in Bucaramanga, the capital of
the Department of Santander.  Its most industrialized centers are the town-s
of Bucaramanga and Barrancabermeja. The Department's contribution to total
value added in Colombia in 1967 was 5.4%, and it provided 4.1% of the total
employment in manufacturing.
2.        Share Capital and Ownership.  In 1969, Valores del Norte and
Banco Santander, two companies belonging to the Santo Domingo group, which
has controlling interests in some of Colombia's largest enterprises, bought
a majority of Santander's shares. At the end of 1971, the group held 617
of the Col$23 million paid-in share capital, 94 private shareholders, includ-
ing the Federacion, owned 27%, and two public shareholders, 11% (Annex 1).
In 1972, share capital increased to Col$24.2 million -- without ant sub-
stantial change in ownership.
3.         Board, Management and Staff.  Santander's board (Annex 2), is
elected for two-year periods and usually meets about once or twice monthly.
Of the seven directors (each with two alternates), the four who attend most
regularly represent the Santo Domingo group. Miost of the board members are
well known local industrialists and businessmen.
4.        The company's by-laws do not define whether it is the board's
or the President's responsibility to approve loans, nor has the board de-
fined a limit for loans the President may approve. In practice, loan
requests are approved by the board although the President sometimes approves
loans which are later confirmed by the board. Moreover, all equity invest-
ments in excess of Col$500,000 are approved by a presidential committee,
comprising the Chairman of the Board, two board members and Santander's
President. Santander should define clearly responsibility for all loan
investment approvals.
5.        Mr. Lievano, Santander's President since inception, is a well-
known and respected Bucaramanga businessman and banker. His intimate
knowledge of local business is very useful for the type of short-term
working capital loans which form almost all of Santander's business. How-
ever, the President does not get deeply involved in the day-to-day operations
of the financiera -- perhaps because he is not very familiar with financial
and technical matters. This means that, as head of a small financiera in-
tending to be involved in long-term lending, he would have to be supported
by suitable staff.



APPENDIX H
Page 2
6.        Annex 3 shows Santander's organization chart.  Santander's small
professional staff of three (of a total staff of thirteen) includes an
economist, a financial analyst and a lawyer. All three are young, have
limited experience, and to work more satisfactorily they would require
close supervision. Santander's staff has inadequate capacity for ap-
praising term lending projects. The financiera considers that it can
rely on the local university for this purpose, particularly for evaluat-
ing engineering matters for which Santander has no staff. While the
university could be used for preparing feasibility studies, Santander
still would have to build up capacity for evaluating these studies.
7.        Appraisal and Follow-up.  Most of Santander's lending has been
short-term working capital loans to existing enterprises, often based only
on the board's knowledge of its borrower and the security provided. Up
to now, Santander has hardly engaged in appraising proposals for long-term
financing. Most of its appraisals for short-term lending contain neither
analyses of the borrowers' financial position nor financial statements.
8.        The main purpose of the few and irregular supervision visits
Santander makes is to check the existence of guarantees. Financial and
operational information is scarce on most of its borrowers. Moreover, the
financiera hardly has the necessary capacity to give technical assistance
to its clients.
9.        Given the lack of experience of Santander's present staff and
the need to provide the President with strong support, it would appear
that a Technical Vice-President with ample experience in project appraisal
and supervision would be necessary. Moreover, the company should try to
engage an engineer with substantial industrial experience.
10.       Procurement and Disbursement Procedures.  At present, the
financiera does not control the procurement practices of its borrowers.
loreover, disbursement procedures do not provide sufficient checks to
ensure that funds will be used for the purposes intended, particularly
in the case of loans for financing construction.
OPERATIONS
11.       Lending Operations.  In 1971, its fifth year of operation,
Santander's loan approvals amounted to Col$79.3 million, compared to
Col$69.6 million in 1970, and Col$60.7 million in 1969, resulting in a
relatively low average increase of 14% yearly (Annex 4). As most of
Santander's financing has been for short-term working capital loans, and
its contracts were concluded immediately before disbursement, disburse-
ment figures equal approvals and commitments for each year. The moderate
growth in disbursements led to a 21% increase in loans outstanding during
1971, from Col$72.8 million to Col$88.1 million.



APPENDIX H
Page 3
12.       Santander's lending has been characterized by a predominance of
small, short-term working capital loans to existing enterprises. Since
inception, the average loan size has been Col$342,000, with 54% of loans
committed under Col$500,000, and the largest loan only Col$6.2 million.
Of loans committed, 78% were for terms of less than two years, and only
5% for more than five years. Of loan commitments, 96% have been for
financing working capital and only 4% for fixed assets, while 99% were
for existing companies and only 1% for new projects. A sector break-
down of loan commitments shows 62% for manufacturing industries and 25%
for construction and real estate.  The bulk of Santander's lending (90%)
has been to the local Department of Santander.
13.       Equity Investments.  In the past, Santander has not been very
promotion-minded, as it has made only seven equity investments (Annex 5),
totaling Col$4.3 million in 1971 (and Col$8.3 million in 1972). Two of
these, Ladrillera Bucaramanga and Caseoducto de Santander, both in opera-
tion, represent the bulk of its portfolio, while the rest are small invest-
ments in promotional companies. At the end of 1971, the equity portfolio
accounted for 5% of Santander's total loan and equity investments and
equalled 13% of its own equity.
14.       Other Operations.  In addition to its regular lending operations,
Santander finances letters of credit and exports, and provides guarantees.
At the end of 1971, letter of credit and export financing outstanding
amounted to Col$5.1 million, and guarantees, to Col$2.6 million.
15.       Policies.  Santander's board has approved the Policy Statement
shown in Annex 8. It contains all the provisions generally usual to devel-
opment finance companies connected with the Bank Group, and is similar to
those of the five financieras. At present, Santander holds more than the
25% -- to which it would normally limit itself - of the voting shares of
two promotion companies. With regard to its 61% ownership of a hotel
promotion company, its share of the hotel, if promoted, will be less than
25%. The purpose of the other company, of which Santander holds 33%, is
to stimulate local industry.
FINANCIAL POSITION AND RESULTS
16.       Resources.  Since inception to the end of 1971, Santander
financed 69% of its operations from its oxwn capital. The bulk of
Santander's term debt comes from BR (Col$16.6 million at the end of
1971) which it mainly employed for medium-term financing. It raised
Col$11.3 million through issues of its own bonds as of end 1971. Of the
US$3.5 million in short-term foreign exchange credit lines available from
13 foreign commercial banks, US$1.4 million were utilized, largely for
working capital financing. Resources which Santander could use for term
lending are from its own equity, its bond issues, and from BR's general funds.



APPENDIX H
Page 4
17.       Financial Structure.  Unaudited income statements and balance
sheets for Santander's first five years, 1967-71, are given in Annex 6.
Total assets at the end of 1971, stood at Col$107.4 million up 25% from
the previous year while the debt to equity ratio increased only slightly
to 2.4:1, due to a Col$2.3 million share capital increase in 1971. The
current ratio was 1.3:1, indicating satisfactory liquidity. As total
assets rose by only 7% to Col$114.6 million in 1972, Santander's debt/
equity ratio only rose to 2.7:1.  Santander's financial structure is
sound.
18.       Income, Expenses and Profitability.  In 1971, Santander's net
profit after taxes was a satisfactory Col$4.4 million, up 29% from
Col$3.4 million in 1970. Profit virtually remained at the 1971 level in
1972. The table below shows the development of income and expenditures,
expressed as percentages of average total assets:
1968     1969      1970     1971
Gross income                           13.2      14.0     14.7      13.8
Financial expenses                      2.2      3.3       4.1       3.9
11.0     10.7      10.6      9.9
Administrative expenses                 4.8       3.0      3.1       2.8
Profit before tax                       6.2       7.7      7.5       7.1
Tax                                     1.9       2.6      2.9       2.4
Prof-t after tax                        4.3       5.1      4.6       4.7
The level of administrative expenses, 2.8% of average total assets in 1971-
72, is somewhat high reflecting the relatively small size of Santander's
operations. In spite of this, the financiera has shown a satisfactory but
not yet very attractive return on investment. Income came almost entirely
from lending operations, with return on average equity portfolio amounting
only to 1.2% in 1971. Net profit before taxes, as a percentage of average
net worth was 22%; in 1970 and 1971, xwhile profit after taxes on year-end
share capital increased from 16.9% in 1970, to 18.7% in 1971.
19.       Quality of Loan and Investment Portfolios.   At the end
of 1971, Santander had loans of Col$2.6 million in arrears of more than
three ronths outstanding with companies with poor or uncertain prospects,
who~_- total loans from the financiera amounted to Col$9.7 million, equiv-
alent to 11% of its loan portfolio. This included Col$1.2 million to
three companies which subsequently went into liquidation. The largest
of the loans in difficulties, of Col$4.5 million, to Ladrillera Bucara-
manga in which Santander has an equity investment was rescheduled; other
reschedulings, amounting to Col$3.4 million, were simply the roll-over
of short-term financing to companies not in financial difficulties. Losses
on the loan portfolio are likely to be small since, with the exception of
Ladrillera Bucaramanga, security is adequate.



APPENDIX H
Page 5
20.       Santander's small equity portfolio (Annex 5), amounting to Col$4.3
million at the end of 1971 includes Col$1.4 million in one manufacturing
company (Ladrillera Bucaramanga), Col$2.1 million in a gas distribution
company and five promotional investments with uncertain prospects, in which
Santander has investments of Col$0.9 million. The brick manufacturer has
lost almost half its equity and is trying to turn around by entering new
lines of production.  The financiera expects to sell its investment in the
gas company, which is operating profitably.
21.       Reserves and Dividend Policy.  Santander, like the other financieras,
has no specific provisions for portfolio losses. It has, however, reserves
for bad debts of Col$169,000 and for losses on equity investments of Col$1.2
million. Moreover, its total reserves (including the legal reserve of
Col$1.8 million, which can only be used if Santander shows a loss in its
income statement) together with an unappropriated surplus, amounted to
Col$9.5 million, or 10% of Santander's loan and investment portfolio. At
present, this is adequate, since likely losses are significantly lower.
22.       Santander retained all earnings through 1969.  With the entry
of the Santo Domingo group as majority shareholder, Santander paid a 10%
dividend on share capital in 1970 and 1971, which amounted to pay-outs of
59% and 54%, respectively. The book value of Santander's shares reached
141% of par at the end of 1971.
23.       Foreign Exchange Risk.  All operations reviewed by the mission
indicate that Santander protects itself adequately against the foreign
exchange risk involved in its operations.
24.       Audit of Accounts.  Santander has no independent external audit.
Its Policy Statement foresees instituting an annual indeperi.dent audit, for
which it is considering using Arthur Young, Clarkson, Gordon & Co., or Price
Waterhouse.
PROSPECTS
25.       Santander's Business Forecast.  Santander projects (Annex 7)
that loan approvals will increase at a rate of 12% to 15% a year in the
period 1972-76, rising from Col$86.8 million in 1971, to Col$129.5 million
in 1976. Somewhat more ambitiously, Santander forecasts equity investments
of Col$4 million a year, largely in companies in which the Santo Domingo
group is in a majority position. The projected moderate growth of lend-
ing, which is somewhat below what Santander has experienced in the past,
should be attainable, particularly if there is sufficiently strengthened
management and staff for processing long-term loans using Bank funds. Re-
sults in 1972 fell short slightly of what had been projected for that year.
26.       Resource Needs.  Santander's projections assume that the
company will annually issue bonds for Col$2-3 million, use Col$5-7 million
of IFF and PIF funds, and place Col$5 million in shares with existing



APPENDIX H
Page 6
shareholders. Santander expects to use Col$24-34 million annually in short-
term credit from foreign commercial banks. Finally, it projects that it
will commit Col$63.8 million in Bank funds during the period. Bank re-
sources to meet 1973 and 1974 commitments would be equivalent to about US$1.0
million. It supports its long-term foreign exchange needs by a reasonable
project pipeline.
27.       Financial Projections.  If Santander's business and resources
develop as forecast, total assets and loan portfolio would grow 15-23%
annually from their Col$107.4 million and Col$90.1 million levels, respec-
tively, in 1971 and more than double during the five-year period. In-
creases in long-term lending, however, would be entirely financed by
Bank funds. Net profit after tax is projected to increase from Col$4.4
million in 1971, to Col$7.3 million in 1976.
28.       Assuming Col$5 million share capital increases yearly, profit
after taxes on year-end share capital would decline from 18.7% in 1971
to 15.4% in 1972 and stay approximately at that level thereafter, while
profit before tax on average equity would drop from 22.2% in 1971 to
20.1% in 1972 and reach 17.2% by 1976. The decline in profitability
would result from the very large yearly capital increases, which would
maintain Santander's present low 2.4:1 leverage practically throughout
the whole forecast period. Administrative expenses would decline from 2.4%
of average total assets in 1971 to 2.3% in 1972 and reach 1.8% by 1976, which
is somewhat slow, owing to the relatively slow growth in projected assets.
29.       Dividends on par value are projected 10% each for 1972 and
1973, equivalent to 60% and 64% pay-out ratios, respectively. Starting
in 1974, the projected dividends are reduced to 8% annually to keep
the pay-out ratios to a maximum of 55%. In view of the declining re-
turns to the shareholders they imply, the capital increases projected
above appear somewhat unrealistic.
30.       Reserves and unappropriated surplus would increase from
Col$9.5 million in 1971, to Col$11.4 million in 1972, and reach
Col$22.3 million in 1976, with their relationship to the total loan
and equity portfolio remaining at about a satisfactory 10% throughout
the period.
31.       Projected debt service coverage would be satisfactory.  Col-
lections on loans are expected to amount to a minimum of 2.6 times the
amount of repayments on debts, and profits before financial expenses
would be more than 1.7 times interest payable.
CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMENDATIONS
32.       Conclusions.  Santander has been extending primarily short-term
working capital loans, based on its knowledge of borrowers or on the security



APPENDIX H
Page 7
provided, and has thereby achieved adequate levels of profitability and
dividends, which, however, are still somewhat low compared to those of
the established financieras. Although a relatively high proportion of its
loan portfolio is with companies in difficulties, most of Santander's
exposure is well secured, and expected losses are therefore small.
Moreover, its reserves are large enough to cover any losses that can be
expected on the loan and equity portfolio.
33.       Prospects of achieving the relatively moderate growth Santander
projects are good, particularly if it has access to Bank funds. However,
this would require tnore effective management and adequate staff to appraise
and supervise long-term investment projects. Lack of financial analysis
and engineering capacity is most pressing. At present, procedures are
deficient, as there is no check on the procurement practices of its
borrowers, and its disbursements procedures are inadequate.
34.       Recommendations.  In view of its insufficiencies in management
and staff regarding appraisal and follow-up and its inadequate procedures,
participation of Santander in the proposed loan is recommended only if a
reappraisal by BR shows that: (a) Santander's management has been strength-
ened by, as a minimum, the addition of a senior staff member, perhaps a
vice-president, with ample experience in project appraisal and supervision;
(b) its staff has adequate capability for appraising and supervising projects;
and (c) adequate procedures, including those for procurement and disbursement,
have been introduced.

APPENDIX H
Annex8
Page 1
COLOMBIA
FIFTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FTNANCTERA DE SANTANDER
Statement of Policies and Procedures
1.        The general policies of the Corporacion Financiera de
Santander shall keep in step with the development programs
of the National Government, especially as regards regional
development.
The Corporaci6nIs efforts shall be devoted to financing the
private sector, within the limits prescribed in its Statutes,
giving preference to the manufacturing industry, provided that
the projectsconcerned are economically, financially and techni-
cally sound.
2.        In the performance of its corporate function, the Corporacion
shall give priority to the following operations:
(a)    Sponsoring of research and studies of industrial,
agriculture, mining, and tourism projects, and
promotion of such projects as are likely to contribute
to economic, regional and national development, provided
that they are likely to show a reasonable return on
capital investment.
(b)    Participation in the capital of enterprises (whether or
not promoted by the Corporacion) or of any other
enterprises in the process of expansion. The Corporacion's
participation may take the form of direct capital
contributions or of loans convertible into stock of the
new enterprise.
(c)    The provision of loans for periods not exceeding fifteen
years to manufacturing, agricultural, mining, transport,
tourism and any other enterprises authorized by the
Colombian Legislature and the Statutes of the Corporacion
and the aim of which is to promote national economic
development.
The Corporacion shall supervise all types of loans granted
for the full term of such loans.
(d)    The promotion of national exports in all possible ways,
using all available credit lines, in order that manufacturers
or producers may have access to foreign exchange credit to
import raw materials or to manufacture exportable products.



APPENDIX H
Annex 8
Page 2
COLOMBIA
FIFTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FTNANCIERA DE SANTANDER
3.        The Corporacion shall promote the capital market as follows:
(a)    By attracting the involvement of foreign capital,
either directly with the Corporacion or with regional
enterprises.
(b)    By seeking credit lines from banks and foreign entities
for use in implementing the Corporacion's general credit
policy.
(c)    By acting as an intermediary for the placement of stocks
or securities issued by private Colombian enterprises
with a view to attracting private savings.
(d)    By issuing its own stocks, bonds or securities of any type
which with a view to attracting regional or national
savings.
h!.       The aim of the Corporacionls financial policies shall always be to
achieve the effective development of the national econony. To
this end its operations shall be governed by the following rules:
(a)    The proportion of its resources used for capital investment
and medium- and long-term loans must constantly increase, with
an emphasis on operations involving some participation in the
capital of an enterprise.
(b)    The amount of loans, capital investments and guarantees granted
by the Corporacion to any one enterprise may not under normal
circumstances, exceed 15% of the Corporacionls net worth.
When necessary, this limit may be exceeded only after
careful study of each case by the Board of Directors of the
Corporacion, and such exceptions may be made only in the case
of enterprises whose economic prospects are absolutely sound
but which are unable to obtain sufficient capital or funds frcm
other sources.
In no case may the amount of loans, investments and guarantees
granted to any one enterprise exceed 25% of the Corporacionts net
worth.
(c)    The Corporaci6n shall adopta prudent dividend distribution policy
that will enable it to build up adequate reserves while making
a fair distribution to its stockholders.
Similarly, the requisite percentage of profits shall be set
aside to reserves, the total of which shall correspond in
quality and amount to the loan and investment portfolios of the
Corporacion.



APPENDIX H
Annex 6
Page 3
COLOMBIA
FITTH FINANCIERA PROJECT
CORPORACION FEINANCIERA DE SANTANDER
(d)    The Corporaci6n may not contract, assume or guarantee
any debt if such an operation would cause the total
indebtedness assumed or guaranteed by the Corporaci6n
to exceed 3 times the Corporacion's net worth.
(e)    The maturities of the Corporacion's assets or portfolio
shall be equal to or, preferably, shorter than those of
its liabilities.
(f)    The minimum amount of each loan or investment operation
in any single enterprise shall be 100,000 pesos, except
under very special circumstances.
(g)    The Corporaci6n shall ensure that its participation in the
capital of any enterprise is never so great as to oblige
it to assume responsibility for managing such enterprise,
i.e. the Corporacionls participation in the subscribed
capital of a given enterprise may not exceed 25% of its
capital.
(h)    The total amount of the Corporaci6nts capital investments
may never exceed its net worth.
(i)    It shall ensure that all operations involving exchange risks
are duly protected.
5.        The Corporaci6n shall seek all possible ways of providing technical
assistance to its clients so that when the latter are preparing
studies or projects they can rely on the Corporaci6nts guidance;
where necessary, the Corporaci6n shall seek the cooperation of other
properly qualified institutions to provide such technical assistance.
6.        The Corporaci6n shall be staffed by personnel properly qualified
to manage its affairs and, in particular by such personnel as may be
required for the economic, financial and technical appraisal, and also
the supervision of its projects.
7.        In addition to its own Auditors, the Corporacion shall hire independent
public accountants to carry out an annual audit of its books and
accounts.
8.        When a decision is to be taken on a matter in which any one of the
directors has an interest or participation, such decision shall be
taken solely by the other directors. The director involved shall
take no part either in the voting or in the discussion.
9.        The Corporaci6n's management shall submit monthly reports to the
Board of Directors, including:
a. Examination of new projects

financial position and operations.
